style="display:none">Saudi journalist</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center">\n<div class="noviewer thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px"><div style="position:relative;width:240px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a scope="row">Date</th><td>\n2&#160;October&#160;2018<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2018-10-02</span>)</span> <br />Some time after 1pm, when Khashoggi entered the Saudi consulate<sup id="cite_ref-NDTV_Fiancee_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV_Fiancee-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Attack type</div></th><td>\nTorture, assassination, and dismemberment (allegedly)<sup id="cite_ref-ES_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-missing_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-missing-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Victim</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi" title="Jamal Khashoggi">Jamal Khashoggi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Perpetrators</th><td>\nAllegedly directed by <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> (<a href="/wiki/Crown_Prince_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Crown Prince of Saudi Arabia">Crown Prince of Saudi Arabia</a>) and led by <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_al-Assiri_(general)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmed al-Assiri (general)">General Ahmed Asiri</a><sup id="cite_ref-saudigazette2013_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saudigazette2013-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-perps_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perps-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Assailants</th><td>\n15-member team brought in from Saudi Arabia<sup id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_6_October_2018_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post_6_October_2018-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Motive</th><td>\nRemoving a prominent dissident and critic of the Saudi leadership (allegedly)<sup id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_6_October_2018_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post_6_October_2018-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Inquiry</th><td>\nOngoing</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi" title="Jamal Khashoggi">Jamal Khashoggi</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Saudi" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi">Saudi Arabian</a> journalist,<sup id="cite_ref-bbcsaudi_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsaudi-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> author, and a former general manager and editor-in-chief of <a href="/wiki/Al-Arab_News_Channel" title="Al-Arab News Channel">Al-Arab News Channel</a>, was killed at the Saudi consulate in Istanbul, Turkey, on 2 October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-speakers_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speakers-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Two anonymous Saudi government officials claimed he had been choked to death by another government operative when an attempt to persuade him to return him to Saudi Arabia went wrong. These claims have been disputed or deemed inevident by the governments of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, with Turkey in particular believing it was premeditated murder.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Khashoggi was visiting the consulate in order to obtain documents related to the marriage he and his fiancee were planning. As no <a href="/wiki/CCTV" class="mw-redirect" title="CCTV">CCTV</a> recorded him exiting,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> he was declared a <a href="/wiki/Missing_person" title="Missing person">missing person</a><sup id="cite_ref-TurkeyToSearch_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TurkeyToSearch-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> amid news reports claiming that he had been killed and <a href="/wiki/Dismember" class="mw-redirect" title="Dismember">dismembered</a> inside.<sup id="cite_ref-ES_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-missing_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-missing-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> An inspection of the consulate, by both Saudi and Turkish officials, took place on 15 October. Turkish officials found evidence of tampering during the inspection and evidence that supported the belief that Khashoggi had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-SearchEvidence_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SearchEvidence-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Initially, the Saudi government claimed he had left alive,<sup id="cite_ref-NDTV_Fiancee_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV_Fiancee-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> but 18 days later admitted he had died inside, claiming this occurred after a fight. Eighteen Saudis were arrested, including the team of 15 which General <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Asiri_(general)" title="Ahmad Asiri (general)">Ahmad Asiri</a> allegedly sent to confront Khashoggi and, if necessary, detain him for a period.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnndeath_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnndeath-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Victim">Victim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Victim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi" title="Jamal Khashoggi">Jamal Khashoggi</a></div>\n<p>Khashoggi was a Saudi journalist,<sup id="cite_ref-bbcsaudi_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsaudi-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> author, and a former general manager and editor-in-chief of <a href="/wiki/Al-Arab_News_Channel" title="Al-Arab News Channel">Al-Arab News Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-speakers_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speakers-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He also served as editor for the Saudi newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Al-Watan_(Saudi_Arabia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Watan (Saudi Arabia)">Al Watan</a></i>, turning it into a platform for Saudi progressives.<sup id="cite_ref-afb_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afb-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Khashoggi fled Saudi Arabia in September 2017 and went into self-imposed exile. He said "The government banned me from Twitter when I cautioned against an overly enthusiastic embrace of then-President-elect Donald Trump."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and he later wrote newspaper articles critical of the Saudi government. Khashoggi had been sharply critical of Saudi Arabia\'s <a href="/wiki/Crown_Prince_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Crown Prince of Saudi Arabia">crown prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a>, and the country\'s <a href="/wiki/King_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="King of Saudi Arabia">king</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Salman of Saudi Arabia">Salman of Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcsaudi_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsaudi-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He also opposed the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disappearance">Disappearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Disappearance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Khashoggi was last seen going inside the main entrance of the Saudi <a href="/wiki/Consulate" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate">consulate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> at around 1 pm on 2 October 2018, in order to obtain a document that proved he was divorced.<sup id="cite_ref-NDTV_Fiancee_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV_Fiancee-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This document would allow him to marry his fianc\xc3\xa9e, Hatice Cengiz, a Turkish citizen, who waited for hours outside.<sup id="cite_ref-NDTV_Fiancee_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV_Fiancee-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_8Oct2018_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_8Oct2018-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As he had not come out by 4 pm, even though the working hours of the consulate were until 3:30 pm, his fianc\xc3\xa9e got in touch with the authorities and reported him missing after the consulate closed.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The Saudi government said that he had left the consulate<sup id="cite_ref-SPA1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPA1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NPR1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> via a back entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Erdo%C4%9Fan_IV" title="Cabinet Erdo\xc4\x9fan IV">Turkish government</a> said that he was still inside, and his fianc\xc3\xa9e and friends said that he was missing.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Turkish authorities have claimed that security camera footage of the day of the incident was removed from the consulate, and that Turkish consulate staff were abruptly told to take a holiday on the day Khashoggi disappeared while inside the building.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/General_Directorate_of_Security_(Turkey)" title="General Directorate of Security (Turkey)">Turkish police</a> investigators told the media that the recordings from the security cameras did not show any evidence of Khashoggi leaving the consulate.<sup id="cite_ref-NH_Thriller_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NH_Thriller-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> A security camera was located outside the consulate\'s front which showed him entering but not leaving, while another camera installed at a preschool opposite the rear entrance of the consulate also did not show him leaving.<sup id="cite_ref-NH_Thriller_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NH_Thriller-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Analysts have suggested that Khashoggi may have been considered especially dangerous by the Saudi leadership because he was not a long-time dissident, but rather a pillar of the Saudi establishment who had been close to its ruling circles for decades, had worked as an editor at Saudi news outlets and had been an adviser to a former Saudi intelligence chief.<sup id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_6_October_2018_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post_6_October_2018-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Investigation">Investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Investigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_(45309197352).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_%2845309197352%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6390" data-file-height="4260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_King_Salman_(45309197352).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> meets with King Salman</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> reported on 11 October that Turkish officials were investigating whether Khashoggi\'s <a href="/wiki/Apple_Watch" title="Apple Watch">Apple Watch</a> would reveal clues as to what happened to him inside the Saudi consulate, examining whether data from the smartwatch could have been transmitted to the <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud</a>, or his personal phone, which was with his fianc\xc3\xa9e, Hatice Cengiz.<sup id="cite_ref-shockingevide_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shockingevide-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the evening of 14 October, <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan">President Recep Tayyip   Erdo\xc4\x9fan</a> and King Salman announced that a deal had been made for a "jointing working group" to examine the case.<sup id="cite_ref-wintour_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wintour-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 15 October the Turkish Foreign Ministry announced that an "inspection" of the consulate, by both Turkish and Saudi officials, would take place that afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> According to an anonymous source from the Attorney General\'s office, Turkish officials found evidence of "tampering" during the inspection, and evidence that supports the belief Khashoggi was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-SearchEvidence_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SearchEvidence-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Turkish President Erdo\xc4\x9fan said that "investigation is looking into many things such as toxic materials and those materials being removed by painting them over".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the same day, after speaking to the Saudi king by phone, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> said that Salman \xe2\x80\x9cdenies any knowledge of whatever may have happened... The denial was very, very strong, It sounded to me like maybe these could have been rogue killers. Who knows?\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-wintour_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wintour-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 16 October, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> "reiterated U.S. concern over Jamal Khashoggi\'s disappearance" in a meeting with King Salman in Riyadh, while also thanking the king for his "commitment to a thorough, transparent investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to anonymous sources, Turkish police have expanded the search, as Khashoggi\'s body may have been disposed of in nearby <a href="/wiki/Belgrad_Forest" title="Belgrad Forest">Belgrad Forest</a> or on farmland in <a href="/wiki/Yalova_Province" title="Yalova Province">Yalova Province</a>, as indicated by the movement of the Saudi vehicles,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/DNA_profiling" title="DNA profiling">DNA tests</a> of samples from the Saudi consulate and the consul\'s residence are being conducted;<sup id="cite_ref-BBCJK_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCJK-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <i>Al Jazeera</i> reported that according to anonymous sources, fingerprints of one of the alleged perpetrators, Salah Muhammad al-Tubaigy, were found in the consulate.<sup id="cite_ref-AJ_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJ-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 22, the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_%C4%B0stanbul" title="Governor of \xc4\xb0stanbul">Governor of \xc4\xb0stanbul</a>\'s office said Khashoggi\'s fiancee, Hatice Cengiz, has 24-hour <a href="/wiki/Police_protection" class="mw-redirect" title="Police protection">police protection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Killing">Killing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Killing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>According to numerous anonymous police sources, the Turkish police believe that Khashoggi was tortured and killed inside the Saudi consulate in Istanbul<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MEE_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEE-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> by a 15-member team brought in from Saudi Arabia for the operation.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> One anonymous police source claimed that the dead body was <a href="/wiki/Dismemberment" title="Dismemberment">"cut into pieces"</a> and quietly moved out of the consulate, and that all of this was "videotaped to prove the mission had been accomplished and the tape was taken out of the country".<sup id="cite_ref-MEE_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEE-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Eye" title="Middle East Eye">Middle East Eye</a> cited an anonymous Saudi to say the <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Squad" title="Tiger Squad">Tiger Squad</a> brought Khashoggi\'s fingers to Mohammad bin Salman in Riyadh as other evidence that the mission was successful.<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye/22oct2018_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye/22oct2018-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 October, Turkish officials pledged to release evidence showing that Khashoggi was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian1_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Yasin Aktay, an adviser to the Turkish president, initially said he believed Khashoggi had been killed in the consulate,<sup id="cite_ref-MEE_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEE-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> but on 10 October he claimed that "the Saudi state is not blamed here", something that a journalist for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> saw as Turkey trying not to harm lucrative trade ties and a delicate regional relationship with Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian2_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian2-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Turkey then claimed to have audio and video evidence of the killing occurring inside the consulate.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> U.S. President Donald Trump said the United States had asked Turkey for the recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> According to "people familiar with the matter", the audio was shared with <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> agents, who declined to publicly comment on it.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> reported on 15 October that Saudi Arabia was about to admit to the killing, but would claim that it was an "interrogation gone bad", as opposed to a targeted death squad killing.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> This claim drew criticism from some, considering that Khashoggi was reportedly dismembered and that his killing was allegedly premeditated, and the circumstances, including the arrival and departure of a team of 15, included forensic specialists presumed to have been present to hide evidence of the crime, on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next day, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Eye" title="Middle East Eye">Middle East Eye</a> reported that, according to an anonymous Turkish source, the killing took about seven minutes and forensic specialist <a href="/wiki/Salah_Muhammed_al-Tubaigy" class="mw-redirect" title="Salah Muhammed al-Tubaigy">Salah Muhammed al-Tubaigy</a>, who had brought along a <a href="/wiki/Bone_cutter" title="Bone cutter">bone saw</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MEE_7minutes_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEE_7minutes-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> cut Khashoggi\'s body into pieces while Khashoggi was still alive, as he and his colleagues listened to music.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The source further claimed that "Khashoggi was dragged from consul general Mohammad al-Otaibi\'s office at the Saudi consulate ... Tubaigy began to cut Khashoggi\'s body up on a table in the study while he was still alive," and "There was no attempt to interrogate him. They had come to kill him."<sup id="cite_ref-MEE_7minutes_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEE_7minutes-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The Turkish pro-government newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Sabah" title="Daily Sabah">Daily Sabah</a></i> reported on 18 October that neighbours to the consul\'s residence had observed an unusual barbecue party, which the paper suggested might have been to smoke-screen the smell from the incineration of the dismembered corpse: "We have been living here for twelve years but I have never seen them having a barbecue party. That day, they had a barbecue party in the garden."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> published reports from anonymous sources that Khashoggi was tortured in front of top Saudi diplomat Mohammad al-Otaibi, Saudi Arabia\'s consul general.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Reuters reported that al-Otaibi left Istanbul for <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a> on 16 October. His departure came hours before his home was expected to be searched in relation to the journalist\'s disappearance.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 October, the Saudi Foreign Ministry reported that a preliminary investigation showed that Khashoggi had died at the consulate while engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Hand-to-hand_combat" title="Hand-to-hand combat">fight</a>, the first Saudi acknowledgement of Khashoggi\'s death.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 21 October, an anonymous Saudi official said Khashoggi had been threatened with drugging and kidnapping by Maher Mutreb, had resisted and was restrained with a <a href="/wiki/Chokehold" title="Chokehold">chokehold</a>, which killed him.<sup id="cite_ref-Rashad_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rashad-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 October, Reuters cited a Turkish intelligence source and a high-ranking Arab in reporting that Saud al-Qahtani, the then-top aide for Mohammed bin Salman, had made a Skype call to the consulate while Khashoggi was held in the room. Qahtani reportedly insulted Khashoggi, who responded in kind. According to the Turkish source, Qahtani then asked the team in the consulate to kill Khashoggi and bring him his head. According to both sources, the audio of the Skype call is currently with Erdogan.<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersSkype_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersSkype-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_perpetrators">Alleged perpetrators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Alleged perpetrators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Al-Waqt news quoted informed sources as saying that <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> had assigned <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_al-Assiri_(general)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmed al-Assiri (general)">Ahmad Asiri</a>, the deputy head of the <a href="/wiki/General_Intelligence_Presidency" title="General Intelligence Presidency">Al-Mukhabarat Al-A\'amah</a><sup id="cite_ref-saudigazette2013_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saudigazette2013-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and the former spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi-led coalition in Yemen</a>, with the mission to execute Khashoggi inside the Saudi consulate in Istanbul. Another military officer with a great deal of experience in dealing with dissidents was the second candidate for the mission.<sup id="cite_ref-perps_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perps-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, Turkish media close to the president published images of what it described as a 15-member "assassination squad" allegedly sent to kill Khashoggi, and of a black van later traveling from the Saudi consulate to the consul\'s home.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 17 October the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Sabah" title="Daily Sabah">Daily Sabah</a></i>, a news outlet close to the Turkish president, published the names and pictures of the 15-member Saudi team apparently taken at passport control.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Additional details about identities were also reported along with their aliases.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> According to one report, seven of the fifteen men suspected of killing Khashoggi are Mohammed bin Salman\'s personal <a href="/wiki/Bodyguard" title="Bodyguard">bodyguards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Daily Sabah</i> outlet named and detailed:\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salah_Mohammed_Al-Tubaiqi_at_Istanbul_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Salah_Mohammed_Al-Tubaiqi_at_Istanbul_airport.jpg/200px-Salah_Mohammed_Al-Tubaiqi_at_Istanbul_airport.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/Salah_Mohammed_Al-Tubaiqi_at_Istanbul_airport.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="225" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salah_Mohammed_Al-Tubaiqi_at_Istanbul_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Salah_Mohammed_Tubaigy" title="Salah Mohammed Tubaigy">Salah Mohammed al-Tubaigy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Atat%C3%BCrk_Airport" title="Istanbul Atat\xc3\xbcrk Airport">Istanbul Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<ul><li>Maher Abdulaziz Mutreb (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb2\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb2 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8</span>&#8206;) (born 1971): a former diplomat in London, was photographed with <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> on trips to <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-straitstimes_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straitstimes-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Salah_Mohammed_Tubaigy" title="Salah Mohammed Tubaigy">Salah Mohammed al-Tubaigy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xb5\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd8\xad \xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1971): the head of the Saudi Scientific Council of Forensics.<sup id="cite_ref-straitstimes_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straitstimes-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Abdulaziz Mohammed Al-Hasawi (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb2\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb2 \xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1987): works as one of <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a>\'s personal bodyguards.<sup id="cite_ref-straitstimes_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straitstimes-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Thaer Ghaleb Al-Harbi (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xab\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa6\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xba\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1979): a member of the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Royal_Guard_Regiment" title="Saudi Royal Guard Regiment">Saudi Royal Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-straitstimes_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straitstimes-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Mohammed Saad Al-Zahrani (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb2\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1988): a member of the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Royal_Guard_Regiment" title="Saudi Royal Guard Regiment">Saudi Royal Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-straitstimes_64-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straitstimes-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Meshal Saad Al-Bostani (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x85\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1987, died 2018): according to <i>Al Jazeera</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant#Air_force_rank" title="Lieutenant">Lieutenant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saudi_Air_Force" title="Royal Saudi Air Force">Saudi Air Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> According to Turkish media, he died in a car accident in Riyadh on return to Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Naif Hassan Al-Arefe (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81 \xd8\xad\xd8\xb3\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1986)</li>\n<li>Mustafa Mohammed Al-Madani (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x85\xd8\xb5\xd8\xb7\xd9\x81\xd9\x89 \xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;)  (born 1961): Allegedly Khashoggi\'s <a href="/wiki/Body_double" title="Body double">body double</a> who made it appear he left the consulate. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.cnn.com/2018/10/22/middleeast/saudi-operative-jamal-khashoggi-clothes/index.html">[1]</a></li>\n<li>Mansur Uthman Abahussein (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x85\xd9\x86\xd8\xb5\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xab\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xad\xd8\xb3\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86</span>&#8206;) (born 1972)</li>\n<li>Waleed Abdullah Al-Shehri (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd8\xaf \xd8\xb9\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x84\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1980)</li>\n<li>Turki Musharraf Al-Shehri (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb1\xd9\x83\xd9\x8a \xd9\x85\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1982)</li>\n<li>Fahad Shabib Al-Balawi (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd9\x81\xd9\x87\xd8\xaf \xd8\xb4\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1985)</li>\n<li>Saif Saad Al-Qahtani (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xb3\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x82\xd8\xad\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1973)</li>\n<li>Khalid Aedh Al-Taibi (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf \xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb6 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1988)</li>\n<li>Badir Lafi Al-Otaibi (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a</span>&#8206;) (born 1973)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="_Saudi_Arabia"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span>Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: \xc2\xa0Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_denial_of_involvement">Initial denial of involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Initial denial of involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Saudi Arabia\'s Crown Prince <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_bin_Salman" title="Mohammad bin Salman">Mohammad bin Salman</a> claimed Khashoggi left the consulate shortly after the visit.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The English-language <i>Arab News</i> on 10 October 2018 reported that the Saudi Ambassador to the U.S., Prince <a href="/wiki/Khalid_bin_Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud" title="Khalid bin Salman bin Abdulaziz Al Saud">Khalid bin Salman</a>, "condemns \xe2\x80\x98malicious leaks and grim rumors\xe2\x80\x99 surrounding Khashoggi disappearance" and that "the reports that suggest that Jamal Khashoggi went missing in the Consulate in Istanbul or that the Kingdom\'s authorities have detained him or killed him are absolutely false, and baseless".<sup id="cite_ref-AN_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AN-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alliance_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alliance-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Saudi Arabia threatened to retaliate "if it is [targeted by] any action".<sup id="cite_ref-punishment_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punishment-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turki_Aldakhil" title="Turki Aldakhil">Turki Aldakhil</a>, the head of <a href="/wiki/Al_Arabiya" title="Al Arabiya">Al Arabiya</a>, the Saudi-owned pan-Arab television based in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, wrote that "If President Trump was angered by $80 oil, nobody should rule out the price jumping to $100 and $200 a barrel or maybe double that figure." However, the Saudi embassy in Washington said Al Dakhil didn\xe2\x80\x99t represent the official position of Saudi Arabia, and <a href="/wiki/Khalid_A._Al-Falih" title="Khalid A. Al-Falih">Khalid A. Al-Falih</a>, the Saudi energy minister, said his country "will continue to be a responsible actor and keep oil markets stable". Saudi Arabia is the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_exports" title="List of countries by oil exports">largest oil exporter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_(30421982117).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_%2830421982117%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5452" data-file-height="3635" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_with_Saudi_Crown_Prince_Mohammed_bin_Salman_(30421982117).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>On 16 October 2018, Saudi Crown Prince met with Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> to discuss the Khashoggi case</div></div></div>\n<p>Saudi Arabia\'s Office of Public Prosecution tweeted that "producing rumors or <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">fake news</a> [that Saudi Arabia\'s government was involved in the disappearance of Khashoggi] that would affect the public order or public security or sending or resending it via social media or any technical means" is punishable "by five years and a fine of 3 million <a href="/wiki/Saudi_riyal" title="Saudi riyal">riyals</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> has suspended a number of <a href="/wiki/Internet_bot" title="Internet bot">bot accounts</a> that appeared to be spreading pro-Saudi tweets about the disappearance of Khashoggi.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Al_Arabiya" title="Al Arabiya">Al Arabiya</a> claimed that reports of Khashoggi\xe2\x80\x99s disappearance inside the Saudi consulate have been pushed by <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>. According to the Saudi daily newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Okaz" title="Okaz">Okaz</a></i>, Qatar has a "50 percent ownership of the <i>[Washington] Post</i> and has influence over its editorial direction". Saudi daily newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Yaum" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Yaum">Al Yaum</a></i> has claimed that members of the death squad were in fact tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Al Jazeera</i> reported on 13 October that "the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> stays silent...there\'s been no official reaction from any Arab government, and hardly any condemnation from Arab media."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_admission_of_involvement">Later admission of involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Later admission of involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 19 October, after 18 days of denial of any involvement with Khashoggi\xe2\x80\x99s disappearance, the Saudi government admitted that he had died in the consulate. An anonymous official added that 15 officials had been sent to confront Khashoggi, that a confrontation occurred when he saw them, which resulted in him trying to flee, causing a fight that ended with him being strangled or choked, and a cover-up of the death. No evidence was provided at the time to support this explanation of events, and no information was given regarding the whereabouts of Khashoggi\xe2\x80\x99s body.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Five high-ranking officials have been removed from their posts<sup id="cite_ref-SPA2_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPA2-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>, including Saudi Royal court adviser Saud al-Qahtani<sup id="cite_ref-SPA3_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPA3-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> and deputy intelligence chief <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Asiri_(general)" title="Ahmad Asiri (general)">Ahmad Asiri</a><sup id="cite_ref-SPA4_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPA4-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>, and 18 Saudis have been detained.<sup id="cite_ref-cnndeath_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnndeath-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Saudi government said that it would need another month to investigate the death.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 October, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> reported that an anonymous government official provided further detail on the death. He said Khashoggi was allegedly threatened with drugging and kidnapping by Maher Mutreb, resisted and was restrained with a chokehold, which killed him. Mustafa Madani then left dressed in Khashoggi\'s clothes to deceive any observers. Khashoggi\'s body was rolled in a carpet and given to a "local cooperator" for disposal. The official provided Saudi documents indicating the operation was part of a wider initiative to bring expatriate dissidents home. The original plan was to keep Khashoggi in an Istanbul safehouse for a period where he would be persuaded to return home or eventually released, and Mutreb had overstepped by threatening a kidnapping. The team then filed a false report indicating they let Khashoggi leave after he warned of Turkish police interference.<sup id="cite_ref-Rashad_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rashad-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 October, Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Adel_al-Jubeir" title="Adel al-Jubeir">Adel al-Jubeir</a> stated in a <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> interview that Prince Mohammed knew nothing of any plan to kill Khashoggi and that the whereabouts of his body remained a mystery.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He called the killing a "murder" and assured Khashoggi\'s family those responsible would be held accountable.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="_Turkey"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span>Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: \xc2\xa0Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>President <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan">Recep Tayyip Erdo\xc4\x9fan</a> demanded that the Saudi government provide proof for their claims that Khashoggi left the consulate alive, something that police CCTV did not capture.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Neil Quilliam, a senior research fellow with <a href="/wiki/Chatham_House" title="Chatham House">Chatham House</a>\'s Middle East and North Africa program, told <i>Business Insider</i> that "The staccato nature of the Turkish response suggests that they were prepared to offer the Saudis a way out of the crisis \xe2\x80\x94 at least provide them with an off-ramp \xe2\x80\x94 but given the Saudi response or lack of it, the authorities continue to share more and more details."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The politician <a href="/wiki/Numan_Kurtulmu%C5%9F" title="Numan Kurtulmu\xc5\x9f">Numan Kurtulmu\xc5\x9f</a>, of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">Justice and Development Party</a>, said that "it\'s not possible for the Saudi administration to wiggle itself out of this crime if it\'s confirmed."<sup id="cite_ref-itv_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itv-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="_United_States"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span>United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: \xc2\xa0United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> expressed concern about the fate of Khashoggi,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a> called on Saudi Arabia "to support a thorough investigation of Mr. Khashoggi\'s disappearance and to be transparent about the results of that investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The reported killing created a bipartisan uproar in <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>, shaking the foundations of the close <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x93United States relations">American-Saudi relationship</a> with calls for suspension of military sales. <a href="/wiki/Lindsey_Graham" title="Lindsey Graham">Lindsey Graham</a>, a senior Republican senator\xe2\x80\x99s reaction was stern, as he said "there would be hell to pay" if Saudi is involved in the murder of Khashoggi. He further added, "If they\'re this brazen it shows contempt. Contempt for everything we stand for, contempt for the relationship."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Murphy" title="Chris Murphy">Chris Murphy</a>, junior <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party" title="Democratic Party">Democratic</a> senator wrote that if the reports are true, \xe2\x80\x9cit should represent a fundamental break in our relationship with Saudi Arabia.\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Murphy also called for at least a temporary halt in military support for the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> can block or modify an arms sale.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Former ambassador to Saudi Arabia <a href="/wiki/Robert_W._Jordan" title="Robert W. Jordan">Robert Jordan</a> said on 12 October that he is 95 percent certain that Saudi Arabia killed Jamal Khashoggi.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_and_Melania_Trump_arrive_to_the_Murabba_Palace,_escorted_by_King_Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud,_May_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Donald_and_Melania_Trump_arrive_to_the_Murabba_Palace%2C_escorted_by_King_Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud%2C_May_2017.jpg/220px-Donald_and_Melania_Trump_arrive_to_the_Murabba_Palace%2C_escorted_by_King_Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud%2C_May_2017.jpg" 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_and_Melania_Trump_arrive_to_the_Murabba_Palace,_escorted_by_King_Salman_bin_Abdulaziz_Al_Saud,_May_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/2017_Riyadh_summit" title="2017 Riyadh summit">Riyadh summit</a>: On 20 May 2017, President Donald Trump signed the <a href="/wiki/2017_United_States%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_arms_deal" title="2017 United States\xe2\x80\x93Saudi Arabia arms deal">United States\xe2\x80\x93Saudi Arabia arms deal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Senator <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">Rand Paul</a> said that he would attempt to force a vote on blocking the future <a href="/wiki/2017_United_States%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_arms_deal" title="2017 United States\xe2\x80\x93Saudi Arabia arms deal">arms sales to Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Senator <a href="/wiki/Bob_Corker" title="Bob Corker">Bob Corker</a>, the chair of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_Foreign_Relations_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate Foreign Relations Committee">Senate Foreign Relations Committee</a>, sent a letter to Trump over Khashoggi\xe2\x80\x99s disappearance. Signed by the entire Committee other than Senator Paul who prepared his own letter, it "instructs the administration to determine whether Khashoggi was indeed kidnapped, tortured, or murdered by the Saudi government and, as the <a href="/wiki/Magnitsky_Act" title="Magnitsky Act">Global Magnitsky Act</a> requires, to respond within 120 days with a determination of sanctions against individuals who may have been responsible".<sup id="cite_ref-alliance_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alliance-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Senator <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a> denounced the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a>, saying that "Saudi Crown Prince Mohammad bin Salman feels emboldened by the Trump administration\xe2\x80\x99s unquestioning support."<sup id="cite_ref-alliance_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alliance-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>President Trump told journalists: "I know [Senators] are talking about different kinds of sanctions, but [the Saudis] are spending $110 billion on military equipment and on things that create jobs for this country."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Trump, in responding specifically to the Senate\'s attempt to block the Saudi arms deal, stated that the blocking of such a deal "would not be acceptable to me".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> While opposing trade sanctions, Trump remained open to the possibility of other forms of what he described as the "severe punishment" of Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-punishment_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punishment-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p><i>The Washington Post</i> reported on 9 October that "the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community" title="United States Intelligence Community">U.S. intelligence</a> intercepted communications of Saudi officials discussing a plan to capture" Khashoggi.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo_2018_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo_2018-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The intercepted communications were regarded as significant because Khashoggi is a <a href="/wiki/Resident_of_the_united_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Resident of the united states">legal resident of the United States</a>, and is therefore entitled to protection. According to <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">NSA</a> officials, the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> was warned of this threat through official intelligence channels.<sup id="cite_ref-Obs_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obs-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Commenting on Pompeo\'s smiling <a href="/wiki/Photo_op" title="Photo op">photo op</a> with Mohammad Bin Salman, an anonymous source close to the Pompeo\'s meeting with Bin Salman said that the photo was not indicating that the meeting had been friendly. According to the CNN, Pompeo told Bin Salman that "his future as king depends on his handling of Khashoggi\'s suspected murder." Pompeo stressed that time is short and went on to tell him "bluntly that if they don\'t, the US will have to deal with this", and "will take action because the world will demand it and that President Trump\'s hand will be forced by the global pressure".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Trump said on 19 October that he "would prefer if there was going to be some form of sanction," adding that "we don\'t use as retribution, canceling $110 billion worth of work, which means 600,000 jobs."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> According to the <i>New York Times</i>, Jamal Khashoggi\'s disappearance comes "at a fraught moment for the Trump administration, which is expected to reimpose harsh <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran" title="Sanctions against Iran">sanctions against Iran</a> on November 5, with the intent of cutting off all <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Iran" title="Petroleum industry in Iran">Iranian oil exports</a>. But to make the strategy work, the administration is counting on its relationship with the Saudis to keep global oil flowing... and to work together on a new policy to contain Iran in the Persian Gulf."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Commenting on the Saudi explanation that Khashoggi died inside the consulate after a fight, Trump said he considered it credible and called the official statement a "good first step".<sup id="cite_ref-cnndeath_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnndeath-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  Several Republican senators, including Marco Rubio, Lindsay Graham, Bob Corker, and Rand Paul have demanded a definitive response from the Trump administration towards Saudi Arabia, with the Trump administration yet remaining unwilling to impose any specific sanctions on the country.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>  In response to Trump\'s apparent faith in the most recently revised official Saudi version of the murder, Washington Post CEO Fred Ryan stated that, "The Saudis cannot be allowed to fabricate a face-saving solution to an atrocity that appears to have been directed by the highest levels of their government."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The New York Times</i> reported that on 16 October, Saudi Arabia transferred $100 million to the American government in return for stabilization efforts in Syria, on the same day U.S. Secretary of State Mike Pompeo arrived in Riyadh for the discussion on Khashoggi with the Saudi king, crown prince and foreign minister. <a href="/wiki/Brett_McGurk" class="mw-redirect" title="Brett McGurk">Brett McGurk</a>, U.S. envoy to the <a href="/wiki/International_military_intervention_against_ISIL" title="International military intervention against ISIL">coalition against ISIL</a>, dismissed any connection between the events, noting the deal had been announced in August.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT$100M_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT$100M-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Saudi Arabia has historically made financial largesse to countries with an aim of gaining support for its foreign policy objectives. <i>The Washington Post</i> reported that Western diplomats also suspect that Saudi Arabia will also be  compensating Turkey with a large scale financial package for agreeing to initiate a joint investigation on Khashoggi.<sup id="cite_ref-WP$100M_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP$100M-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="_Canada"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span>Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: \xc2\xa0Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a> has said that he has "real concerns" about the disappearance of Khashoggi.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Chrystia_Freeland" title="Chrystia Freeland">Chrystia Freeland</a> "reaffirmed (Canada\'s) commitment to defending <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of expression</a> and protection of the free press" and raised the issue directly with her Saudi counterpart, calling for "a thorough, credible and transparent investigation into the serious allegations about Mr. Kashoggi\'s disappearance". She added that "Canada remains very troubled by (his) disappearance."<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party" title="New Democratic Party">New Democratic Party</a> has called for an end to Canada\'s arms deals with Saudi Arabia<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>, which Freeland has indicated would not be revisited.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Saudi Arabia released its official description of the death of Khashoggi, <a href="/wiki/Global_Affairs_Canada" title="Global Affairs Canada">Global Affairs Canada</a> released a statement condemning Khashoggi\'s killing by Saudi Arabia saying "the explanations offered to date lack consistency and credibility". The statement reiterates Canada\'s call for a thorough investigation and for \xe2\x80\x9cthose responsible for the killing (to) be held to account and (to) face justice.\xe2\x80\x9d <sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_reactions">Other reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="_Europe"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" />&#160;</span>Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: \xc2\xa0Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Germany: <a href="/wiki/Norbert_R%C3%B6ttgen" title="Norbert R\xc3\xb6ttgen">Norbert R\xc3\xb6ttgen</a>, chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> parliamentary foreign affairs committee, criticized Donald Trump\xe2\x80\x99s comments, "The decisive factor now is the behaviour of the U.S. president, who basically told the crown prince, we are giving you free rein as long as you buy enough weapons and other things from us."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> However, <i>The Washington Post</i> on 15 October reported that "While Britain, France and Germany issued a joint statement over the weekend in which they called for a \xe2\x80\x9ccredible investigation,\xe2\x80\x9d none of the three countries have gone beyond the remarks so far voiced by the White House. If anything, they\xe2\x80\x99ve been even less vocal. While U.S. pressure on Trump has been bipartisan, in Europe, calls to punish Saudi Arabia have mostly come from opposition parties. ... While German observers have lashed out at Trump for refusing to punish the Saudis, German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>\xe2\x80\x99s spokesman said the Khashoggi case and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Angela_Merkel_government#Middle_East" title="Foreign policy of the Angela Merkel government">German exports to Riyadh</a> were "two unrelated things"."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Germany stated the Saudi explanation as \xe2\x80\x9cinadequate\xe2\x80\x9d and Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Heiko_Maas" title="Heiko Maas">Heiko Maas</a> questioned if weapons should be sold to Saudi Arabia by countries. France and the European Union requested for a detailed investigation on the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters21OctTrump_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters21OctTrump-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span>Spain: The foreign ministry said t was also "upset" by the statements of Saudi Arabia regarding the killing of Khashoggi, according to written statement from Spain\'s Ankara Embassy on Monday. The statement said the perpetrators of the incident should pay the price of it before justice "after a wide-scoped and transparent investigation" and also offers their condolences to Khashoggi\'s family.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPJPN_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPJPN-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>United Kingdom: British Foreign Secretary <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Hunt" title="Jeremy Hunt">Jeremy Hunt</a> met the Saudi ambassador and warned Saudi Arabia that the long-term <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Saudi Arabia\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations">friendship between the UK and Saudi Arabia</a> depends on "shared values".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Shadow_First_Secretary_of_State" title="Shadow First Secretary of State">Shadow First Secretary of State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emily_Thornberry" title="Emily Thornberry">Emily Thornberry</a>, criticized <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>\'s government\'s response to Khashoggi\'s disappearance as \'too little, too late\'.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Thornberry was critical of UK-Saudi relations, saying: "Imagine how this government would have reacted if either <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> had abducted \xe2\x80\x93 and in all likelihood murdered \xe2\x80\x93 one of their dissident journalists within the sovereign territory of another country."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<dl><dd>Labour Party\'s leader <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a> and Shadow Secretary of State for International Trade <a href="/wiki/Barry_Gardiner" title="Barry Gardiner">Barry Gardiner</a> called for the suspension of UK arms sales to Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Corbyn also called for an international investigation into the murder of Khashoggi and Saudi\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations_during_the_Yemeni_Civil_War_(2015%E2%80%93present)" title="Human rights violations during the Yemeni Civil War (2015\xe2\x80\x93present)">war crimes in Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Vince_Cable" title="Vince Cable">Vince Cable</a> said: "This situation gets murkier and murkier. The Government should have already suspended arms export licences to Saudi Arabia given the outrages in Yemen. This reinforces the argument for loosening the bonds to the regime."<sup id="cite_ref-itv_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itv-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>On 19 October the former chief of the <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">Secret Intelligence Service</a> (MI6), <a href="/wiki/John_Sawers" title="John Sawers">John Sawers</a>, told the BBC that all the evidence suggested Crown Prince Salman was behind the death of Khashoggi, and that the theory that rogue elements in the Saudi military were responsible was "blatant fiction".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_statements">Joint statements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Joint statements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></span><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" responding to the statement from Saudi Arabia confirming the death of Khashoggi in a fist fight, UK, France and Germany issued a joint statement expressing shock and condemning the killing of Khashoggi, saying there is an "urgent need for clarification of exactly what happened".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian3_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian3-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The statement mentioned the Saudi explantation of the events and added "There remains an urgent need for clarification of exactly what happened... beyond the hypotheses that have been raised so far in the Saudi investigation, which need to be backed by facts to be considered credible."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCShock21October2018_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCShock21October2018-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> British foreign minister Hunt, spoke to his Saudi counterpart <a href="/wiki/Adel_al-Jubeir" title="Adel al-Jubeir">Adel al-Jubeir</a>, on 21 October to convey the British view that the explanation provided was not entirely credible.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_world"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Arab_League.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span> Arab world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Killing_of_Jamal_Khashoggi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Arab world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Eye" title="Middle East Eye">Middle East Eye</a> reported on 15 October that "Largely silent until Sunday, <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab</a> leaders come out publicly in support of kingdom after US President Donald Trump threatens \'severe punishment\'."<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, "It is totally unacceptable, in the context of relations between countries, to wave economic sanctions as a policy or tool to achieve political goals."<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="900" />&#160;</span>Bahrain: The Foreign ministry released a statement that Saudi Arabia is "the essential foundation for the security and stability of the Arab and Islamic worlds and the solid foundation and strong pillar of stability in the region".<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" spokesman, said  that "Egypt reaffirms its support for the kingdom in its efforts and positions dealing with this event."<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye_136-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Flag_of_Lebanon.svg/45px-Flag_of_Lebanon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span>Lebanon: Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Saad_Hariri" title="Saad Hariri">Saad Hariri</a> said in a statement that he stood in solidarity with Saudi Arabia "in the face of the campaigns targeting it".<sup id="cite_ref-middleeasteye_136-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-middleeasteye-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> leader, <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a> said in a speech: "I tell the Saudi rulers that now is the right time to take a bold and brave stance and stop the war on Yemen... The international cover for their war on Yemen has started to crumble, especially after [Khashoggi] incident. The kingdom\'s image in the world has never been worse throughout 100 years."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Rami_George_Khouri" title="Rami George Khouri">Rami George Khouri</a>, a professor of journalism at the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">American University of Beirut</a>, "The case of Jamal Khashoggi, unfortunately, is only the tip of the iceberg... it would only be the most dramatic example of a trend that has been ongoing for at least 30 to 40 years, but which has escalated under [Saudi crown prince Mohammad bin Salman]".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder"
